item_5.note: Case: Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-963]. Client: Ashlee Williams. Re: Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson (Floyd 22D03-2501-CT-000157).

The record consists of a sequence of email exchanges between counsel regarding scheduling depositions in the case Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson. The involved parties include W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, and Zachary Reichle, Associate at Stoll Keenon Ogden PLLC, along with the named plaintiffs Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore, whose MVA claims occurred on 8/29/2023. The CC list in the emails includes Dennis Cantrell and Janet Weile, as well as filevine project email addresses for Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore, plus a filevine contact for Janet Weile. The emails also include standard attorney-client confidentiality notices.

The first substantive thread in the record, dated October 17, 2025, shows Zach Reichle requesting the availability of the plaintiffs for depositions in November or December. He also notes a mediation deadline of January 31, 2026 and that the parties had agreed to Larry Church as mediator at the Case Management Conference on July 29, 2025. Reichle explains that their office is booked throughout January and early February of the following year, so mediation would likely be scheduled for late February or March. He adds that this scheduling should not present an issue for the Court, given that trial is not set to occur until December 2026, but he asks to be notified of the office’s position.

A subsequent email, dated October 22, 2025, from Bryce Koon confirms that his clients are available for depositions on any date during November 3–7, 2025, and asks that if any of those dates work, they can get the scheduling set.

On October 24, 2025, Reichle replies that November 6 and November 7 work for his office. He asks whether scheduling all three depositions consecutively would be feasible, proposing 9:00 a.m. to noon on November 7 as an option. He also notes that they have no issue with holding the depositions on separate days if necessary.

On October 29, 2025, Bryce Koon follows up with a reply confirming that the plaintiffs are available for depositions on the 7th. He indicates that Julmonzhae Moore and Ashlee Williams are available, with Moore’s availability in the afternoon, so it would be best to start with her deposition first. He states that Mr. Ward would let him know by tomorrow whether he will be available on November 7 and promises to inform the recipient as soon as he hears back.

In addition to these scheduling emails, the record contains earlier correspondence from May 2025. A May 5, 2025 message from Bryce Koon to Dennis Cantrell and Zach Reichle is present, but its content is truncated in the record. A May 19, 2025 email from Zach Reichle requests an additional thirty days to finalize Defendant’s responses to Plaintiffs’ discovery requests, explaining that the current due date was June 4 and proposing a new due date of July 7 to accommodate the extension, noting that June 4 plus thirty days would land on July 4 and the following two days were the weekend. A reply from Zach’s counterpart on May 19, 2025 at 1:43 p.m. states, “July 7th is fine.” The May 19, 2025 10:08 a.m. email from Zach Reichle further documents the same discovery-extension discussion and reiterates his contact details and confidentiality notices.

Throughout these exchanges, the parties discuss aligning deposition timing with anticipated mediation, considering preferences for the order and pacing of depositions, and ensuring that the plaintiffs’ availability accommodates multiple depositions within the proposed windows. The plan evolving from the communications is to proceed with depositions in early November 2025, prioritizing Julmonzhae Moore for the first deposition given her afternoon work schedule, with Ashlee Williams and Dewayne Ward to follow, contingent on Ward’s confirmation of his availability for November 7.

All communications in the record include standard confidentiality language indicating that the messages are intended only for the named recipients and may contain privileged information; recipients are advised not to disclose or forward the content if received in error. The sender details and firm affiliations appeared consistently, with The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information listed for Bryce Koon and Stoll Keenon Ogden LLP’s contact information listed for Zach Reichle, alongside the affected clients and CC recipients.

item_6.note: In the matter of Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson (Floyd 22D03-2501-CT-000157), counsel engaged in coordinating depositions for the plaintiffs—Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore—who are clients in this motor vehicle accident case filed on August 29, 2023. The correspondence began with W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, and involved Zachary Reichle, Esq., an associate at Skofirm, along with several other recipients and Filevine project email addresses linked to the three clients. The exchanges also included Janet Weile of Skofirm and a standard attorney-client confidentiality notice on each message.

The scheduling discussion began with a May 19, 2025 email in which Bryce Koon indicated that July 7 would work for him and invited any further needs or information. This initial exchange set the stage for later deposition planning, though the concrete scheduling discussion would resume later in the year.

On October 17, 2025, Zach Reichle asked counsel to provide the plaintiffs’ availability in November or December for depositions. He also noted a mediation deadline of January 31, 2026 and stated that the parties were agreeable to Larry Church as mediator at the Case Management Conference held on July 29, 2025. Reichle explained that, due to prior bookings in January and early February, mediation would likely take place in late February or March, although he expected this would not be an issue for the Court given that trial was not set until December 2026. He concluded by thanking counsel.

Bryce Koon replied on October 22, 2025, informing Reichle that his clients were available for depositions on any date during November 3 through November 7, and asking to be advised which dates would work so scheduling could proceed.

On October 24, 2025, Reichle responded that November 6 and 7 would work for his office. He proposed scheduling all three depositions consecutively, from 9:00 a.m. to Noon on November 7, but said there was no issue with holding the depositions on separate days if necessary.

A subsequent message from Bryce Koon on October 29, 2025 at 1:08 p.m. reiterated that his clients were available for depositions on any date during November 3 through November 7. He asked that, if any of those dates would work, Reichle’s side should inform him so they could get things scheduled.

Later that same day, at 1:43 p.m., Bryce wrote that he had confirmed with Ms. Moore and Ms. Williams that they were available on November 7. He noted that Ms. Moore works that afternoon, so he suggested starting with her deposition. He added that Mr. Ward had said he would inform him by tomorrow whether he would be available on November 7, and he pledged to relay any updates as soon as he received them. Bryce’s message also included the standard confidentiality disclaimer and the email signature for The Whaley Law Firm.

Shortly thereafter, at 1:49 p.m., Reichle replied: the plan was to issue notices for Ms. Moore’s deposition beginning at 9:00 a.m. on November 7, with Ms. Williams’s deposition to follow at 11:00 a.m. He added that Mr. Ward was available the week of November 10 if November 7 did not work for him.

The thread, which includes CC’d recipients such as Dennis Cantrell and the Filevine project addresses for Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore, as well as Janet Weile at Skofirm, reflects a concerted effort across counsel to finalize the deposition schedule. The messages also contain standard attorney-confidentiality notices.

In summary, the parties are coordinating depositions for Ashlee Williams, Julmonzhae Moore, and Dewayne Ward in the Williams-Ward-Moore v. Robinson case. The tentative plan, settled by communications in late October 2025, was to hold Ms. Moore’s deposition first on November 7 beginning at 9:00 a.m., followed by Ms. Williams’s deposition at 11:00 a.m., with Mr. Ward’s availability to be determined if November 7 proved unsuitable for him. The clients’ overall availability was framed around the November 3–7 window, with broader availability discussed for the week of November 10 if needed, and a mediation deadline of January 31, 2026, with Larry Church proposed as mediator and mediation possibly pushed to late February or March 2026 due to scheduling constraints.

item_8.note: Case: Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson (Floyd 22D03-2501-CT-000157). The matter is a motor vehicle collision case filed on August 29, 2023, naming three plaintiffs: Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore. The current communications concern scheduling and discovery in the case, with counsel from The Whaley Law Firm representing the plaintiffs and Stoll Keenon Ogden PLLC representing the defense. The plaintiffs’ file includes Filevine project email addresses for each client: Ashlee Williams MVA 8/29/23, Dewayne Ward MVA 8/29/2023, and Julmonzhae Moore MVA 8/29/2023, along with Janet Weile on the defense side.

On May 5, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent counsel a message to Zachary Reichle of SKO (with Dennis Cantrell and the three Filevine addresses copied) attaching Plaintiffs’ First Set of Discovery, including a Word copy for convenience, and inviting questions if any arose. The message was part of the ongoing discovery process and carried the usual attorney-client confidentiality notice typical of such electronic communications.

A few weeks later, on May 19, 2025, Reichle requested an extension to finalize the defense responses to Plaintiffs’ discovery requests, asking for an additional thirty days. He noted that the current due date was June 4, and that extending thirty days would push the response due date to July 7 (since June 4 plus thirty days would land on July 4, with the following weekend days). Bryce Koon replied later that day, confirming that July 7 would be acceptable. The exchange also displayed the parties’ standard contact details for The Whaley Law Firm and SKO, and included the same confidentiality notice.

In a later thread, Reichle referenced a mediation deadline of January 31, 2026, and indicated that he believed the parties had agreed to Larry Church as mediator at the Case Management Conference held on July 29, 2025. He proposed that, if acceptable to the plaintiffs’ office, they could contact Larry Church’s office to determine his availability. He cautioned that the defense team was booked throughout January and early February of the following year, making mediation likely to occur in late February or March, but he did not anticipate any issue with the Court given that trial is not set until December 2026. This message also contained Reichle’s signature block with his role as Associate at SKO and contact information, and reaffirmed the confidentiality notice.

Later, on October 17, 2025, Reichle again reached out to request the scheduling of Plaintiffs’ depositions and asked for the plaintiffs’ availability in November or December. He also reiterated the January 31, 2026 mediation deadline and the use of Larry Church as mediator, referencing the July 29, 2025 Case Management Conference where that mediator arrangement was noted. He warned of limited availability in January and early February and indicated that late February or March would likely be required for mediation, while expressing that this would not be a problem for the Court since trial remains set for December 2026.

Finally, on October 22, 2025, Bryce Koon replied that the plaintiffs were available for depositions on any date within November 3–7, 2025, and invited the defense to select a date within that window to proceed with scheduling. He included his professional contact information and reaffirmed the standard confidentiality notices that accompany such correspondence.

In sum, the case involves three plaintiffs in a Floyd County motor vehicle collision matter, with discovery ongoing and a schedule that includes an extension to discovery responses (defense due July 7, 2025), a mediation deadline of January 31, 2026 with Larry Church as mediator (to be confirmed with his office), and a depositions window for the plaintiffs set for November 3–7, 2025, as the parties work toward finalizing discovery and mediation in advance of a trial not set until December 2026.

item_32.note: Case: Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-108]. Client: Ashlee Williams.

This matter concerns Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson (Floyd 22D03-2501-CT-000157). The named client is Ashlee Williams, with the underlying event dated August 29, 2023, and the caption reflecting the Floyd County docket number. The communications summarized below occurred between The Whaley Law Firm and Stoll Keenon Ogden PLLC, with multiple recipients and filevine project email addresses copied on the correspondence.

On May 5, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Dennis Cantrell and Zachary Reichle at SKO, with Sarena Tuttle and several “Filevine Project Email Address” recipients CC’d. The subject line was Williams, Ward, Moore v. Robinson (Floyd 22D03-2501-CT-000157). In the body of the message, Bryce attached Plaintiffs’ First Set of Discovery along with the associated notice filed that day, and he noted that a Word copy was included for convenience. He invited any questions and closed with his signature and contact information for The Whaley Law Firm, including the firm’s address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone number [PHONE-877]; and fax number [PHONE-876]. The CC list included Sarena Tuttle; Ashlee Williams MVA 8/29/23 – Filevine Project Email Address ([EMAIL-875]); Dewayne Ward MVA 8/29/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address ([EMAIL-874]); Julmonzhae Moore MVA 8/29/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address ([EMAIL-113]); and Janet Weile ([EMAIL-114]). The message contained the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer typical of electronic correspondence.

Later, on May 19, 2025 at 1:43:26 PM (GMT-04:00), Bryce Koon replied: “Good afternoon counsel, July 7th is fine with me. If you need anything else from me, please let me know.” This message again carried Bryce’s professional signature and the firm’s confidentiality notice.

Earlier that same day, at approximately 10:08 AM, Zachary Reichle of SKO sent a separate email to counsel requesting an extension: “Good morning, counsel, May we have an additional thirty days to finalize Defendant’s responses to Plaintiffs’ discovery requests? Currently, the responses are due June 4th. With the additional thirty days, the responses would become due July 7th (thirty days from June 4th lands on July 4th and the following two days are the weekend).” He signed with his contact information (Associate, SKO), and the message included SKO’s confidentiality notice. The email thread shows further that SKO’s communications continued to include standard privilege and confidentiality provisions.

In sum, the record shows:
- May 5, 2025: Bryce Koon transmitted Plaintiffs’ First Set of Discovery and a notice, attached as well as a Word copy, to opposing counsel and cc’d recipients, including filevine addresses for Ashlee Williams, Dewayne Ward, and Julmonzhae Moore, plus Janet Weile, with Bryce’s firm details and a standard confidentiality disclaimer.
- May 19, 2025 (1:43 PM): Bryce indicated that July 7th was acceptable.
- May 19, 2025 (approx. 10:08 AM): Zach Reichle requested a 30-day extension to July 7 for Defendant’s discovery responses, explaining the calculation around weekends and the June 4 deadline. His message also included his SKO contact details and a confidentiality notice.

item_56.note: Case: Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-211]. Client: Ashlee Williams (DOB [DOB-985]). Re: Certified Medical Records & Billing Request - Ashlee Williams [DOB-985].

On November 26, 2024, a series of email exchanges took place between Fax Legal and The Whaley Law Firm regarding a request for Certified Medical Records and billing for the above-named client. The thread opens with Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sending an afternoon message that Good afternoon, and that an attached request for Certified Medical Records & Billing for the referenced client was included, with additional information in the attachments.

Fax Legal later replied that there appears to be a certified copy already on file and asked whether a new copy was needed, indicating there had been no change since the last request. In a subsequent message, Sarena apologized for pages not all attaching and confirmed that the attached material should now be considered. She stated: Yes, please send a Certified Copy of any and all medical records & billing, and noted that a Certified copy is required for filing with the local circuit court.

Fax Legal then raised the matter of a certification fee, asking: There is a $10 fee for certification of records. Is your firm ok with that? In response, Sarena indicated that the fee is acceptable and asked that Fax Legal attach a copy of the invoice so she could forward it for payment processing.

Throughout the thread, Sarena provided updated contact information for The Whaley Law Firm, including the firm’s address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-212]; office line [PHONE-213] ext 104; and the new email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (note the “PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS” line).

The communications culminated with a closing message from Fax Legal, dated November 26, 2024, at 21:23:31 +0000, wishing a great day and a Happy Thanksgiving.

item_83.note: Initial client contact on September 27, 2024, with Sarena regarding Ashlee Williams’ motor vehicle accident settlement status. The client stated that everyone had signed about two weeks earlier. See JC note to AW about check timing. The releases were returned and signed on 09/19, and the Settlement Statement was signed on 09/12.

I advised the client that the Settlement Statement verifies she has accepted the Settlement Agreement but only triggers acceptance of the offer. Once the Release is signed and returned to the insurer, they have 30-45 days to issue a check. While some insurance companies will process this quicker to close the file, some will wait the full 30 days. Her specific 30-day clock started on 09/19, so the insurer has until 10/19 to mail the check. The client is welcome to call back next Friday to check for the check, and I would be happy to check with FG. JC works off-site and does not have direct access to current mail. The client expressed understanding and appreciated the explanation.

item_107.note: On August 13, 2024, in the case identified as Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-379], concerning client Ashlee Williams and co-claimants Julmonzhae Moore, Naomi Robinson, and Daquan Graham (Claim #: 054658453-01), a series of emails circulated among the parties’ counsel. The subject line referenced the four claimants and the claim number, and the message was from Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm in Louisville, Kentucky. In the body of his message, he asked, “Great. James?” and signed with his contact information, followed by copies to Scott Stout and other recipients, including Ashlee Williams and several attorney representatives. Scott Stout, identified as with Stout & Heuke Law Office, responded in a subsequent thread noting that he had authority to settle Daquan Graham, and he provided the firm’s Louisville addresses and contact numbers for both the downtown and other offices, indicating an active participation in settlement discussions.

Earlier communications, dating from August 1, 2024, reflect an inquiry about settlement authority: Aaron Whaley asked James Kamensky, Esq., whether James had authority to resolve Daquan Graham and Naomi Robinson, while Aaron himself stated he had authority to resolve Ashlee Williams and Julmonzhae Moore. The August 1 message also included Aaron’s sign-off with his firm’s address and phone number.

The chain also shows substantial back-and-forth in July 2024 regarding authority and insurance coverage. On July 10, 2024, James Kamensky asked whether Naomi Robinson had underinsured motorist (UIM) coverage, noting that underinsured coverage appeared to be important and requesting a point of contact for UofL records. James added that Naomi did not appear to have underinsured coverage, and he attached related materials. Aaron Whaley replied on July 15, 2024 that there was no access to any underinsured coverage either. James then acknowledged the point but indicated he needed a few days to confer with the client and assess medical billing. Scott Stout subsequently chimed in on July 15, clarifying that he had misread something and asked that the previous message be disregarded.

In the same July 15, 2024 window, Aaron Whaley provided a proposed breakdown of the settlements based on total medical bills. He listed the following allocations: Naomi Robinson $15,383.44; Ashlee Williams $16,503.23; Julmonzhae Moore $14,734.08; and Daquan Graham $3,379.25. He presented the underlying figures underlying these allocations, showing the raw totals used for each claimant (Naomi Robinson 32,754; Ashlee Williams 35,138.24; Julmonzhae Moore 31,371.4; Daquan Graham 7,195) and the calculated shares (0.307668781 for Naomi, 0.[PHONE-380] for Ashlee, 0.[PHONE-381] for Julmonzhae, and 0.06758493251 for Daquan), which produced the final dollar amounts cited.

Earlier in the chain, on July 12, 2024, Aaron Whaley wrote “Circling back on this. Would like to get this resolved as soon as possible.” James Kamensky followed with an update indicating that hospital records and billing were pending, but collateral source information showed total billed amounts of $26,554 plus $6,200 at a rehab clinic, and he asked about specials for the other claimants, whether there had been significant injuries, and whether UIM would apply. Aaron’s response reaffirmed a sense of urgency to resolve the matter, while James’s prior messages underscored the need to verify medical billing and collateral sources. The July 12 exchange also included the standard attorney–client privilege notices typical of such communications.

Before these exchanges, James Kamensky had asked in June 2024 whether the team had a good point of contact for the University of Louisville records, indicating that he would relay the matter to their records team. This shows ongoing coordination with medical providers and institutions as part of evaluating the case's settlement value and collateral sources.

Overall, the record captures an ongoing effort through mid-2024 to negotiate settlements among multiple claimants, determine authority to settle each individual claim, assess underinsured coverage and collateral sources, and finalize a proportional distribution of settlement proceeds based on the total medical bills. By August 13, 2024, Scott Stout stated he had authority to settle Daquan Graham, and Aaron Whaley followed with a prompt to involve James Kamensky on related authority matters, signaling continued progress toward resolving the four-claim file. The communications include standard privileged notices and reflect the professional interactions among the counsel and the clients involved.

The correspondence in question centers on settlement discussions for the four claimants related to the motor vehicle accident. The chain begins with communications among Ashlee Williams’s counsel and related counsel as they assess representation and authority to resolve the matter.

On July 12, 2024, James Kamensky, Esq., sent a message noting that hospital records and billing were still pending. He reported that collateral source information had been received showing total billed amounts of $26,554, plus $6,200 at a rehabilitation clinic. He asked for input on the other claimants’ specials, whether any of the injuries were significant, and whether applicable underinsured motorist coverage (UIM) existed. Later on July 12, 2024, in a following thread, James asked about the status of underinsured coverage for the claimants, indicating that Naomi Robinson did not have underinsured coverage, and he referenced an attachment. This was followed by further exchanges through July 15 and July 17 addressing authority to resolve different claimants and the status of insurance coverage.

On July 15, 2024 at 1:00 PM, Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm provided a proposed breakdown based on total medical bills for the four claimants:
- Naomi Robinson: $15,383.44
- Ashlee Williams: $16,503.23
- Julmonzhae Moore: $14,734.08
- Daquan Graham: $3,379.25

He included supporting figures in a line-item format showing the underlying numbers used to compute these totals (Naomi Robinson with a total of 32,754 and a factor of 0.307668781 producing 15,383.43905; Ashlee Williams with 35,138.24 and a factor of 0.[PHONE-589] producing 16,503.23543; Julmonzhae Moore with 31,371.4 and a factor of 0.[PHONE-588] producing 14,734.07889; Daquan Graham with 7,195 and a factor of 0.06758493251 producing 3,379.246626).

At 1:24 PM on July 15, 2024, Scott Stout (Stout & Heuke Law Office) replied: “Wait. I misread that. I see where I made the mistake. My apologies. Please disregard.” This indicated a correction to the prior proposed figures or assumptions.

Earlier that same day, at 10:55 AM, James Kamensky had asked whether Naomi Robinson’s claim involved underinsured coverage and requested the attached documentation, indicating that Naomi might not have underinsured coverage and seeking confirmation on that point.

On July 17, 2024 at 12:09 PM, Aaron Whaley responded: “We do not have access to any under insured coverage either.” At 12:10 PM, James Kamensky replied that he needed a few days to confer with his client and assess medical billing, but would let the other side know his position.

Case overview and proposed allocation
The case is titled Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-442] and involves client Ashlee Williams. The correspondence concerns four claimants: Naomi Robinson, Ashlee Williams, Julmonzhae Moore, and Daquan Graham, under Claim #: 054658453-01. The initial note documents a correspondence dated Monday, July 15, 2024 at 12:59:43 PM (-0400) from Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm ([EMAIL-543]) to James Kamensky, Esq. ([EMAIL-444]), with cc’s to Lexi Graham, Scott Stout, Robert Elliott, and Ashlee Williams ([EMAIL-445]). The subject line is “Re: Ashlee Williams, Julmonzhae Moore, Naomi Robinson, Daquan Graham / Claim#:054658453-01.”

A proposed breakdown based on total medical bills is as follows:
- Naomi Robinson: $15,383.44
- Ashlee Williams: $16,503.23
- Julmonzhae Moore: $14,734.08
- Daquan Graham: $3,379.25

The accompanying calculations are listed as:
- Naomi Robinson 32754 0.307668781 15383.43905
- Ashlee Williams 35138.24 0.[PHONE-540] 16503.23543
- Julmonzhae Moore 31371.4 0.[PHONE-539] 14734.07889
- Daquan Graham 7195 0.06758493251 3379.246626

Ongoing discussion about hospital records, bills, and coverage
In a reply dated Friday, July 12, 2024, at approximately 2:05 PM (the time is recorded as 2:05?PM in the record), James Kamensky, Esq. wrote that hospital records and billing were pending. He noted that collateral source information showed a total billed amount of $26,554 plus $6,200 at a rehab clinic. He asked for input on several topics: what about the other claimants’ specials, whether the injuries were significant, and whether applicable UIM (uninsured/underinsured motorist) coverage applied.

James Kamensky’s signature and contact details follow in the record, including multiple office locations (Columbia, SC; Birmingham, AL; Indianapolis, IN) and mailing address in Boca Raton, FL, with the usual attorney–client and/or work product privileged material disclaimer.

On June 24, 2024 at 4:21 p.m. Eastern Time, Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm—located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222 and reachable at [PHONE-461]—sent an email asking, “Any progress on this?” The message was addressed to James Kamensky, Esq., and copied to Ashlee Williams and several other involved counsel and parties, including Robert Elliott of Liberty Mutual, Lexi Graham, and Scott Stout, among others. item_143.note: This case note concerns Ashlee Williams in the motor vehicle accident matter titled Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-490], with client Ashlee Williams and related parties Julmonzhae Moore, Naomi Robinson, and Daquan Graham. The formal claim number is 054658453-01. The communications below were exchanged among the firm’s attorney Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm, James Kamensky (Kamensky & Patteson, LLP), and the supporting team, including Lexi Graham, Scott Stout, Robert Elliott, and Ashlee Williams, across March through May 2024.

On May 13, 2024, Aaron Whaley sent an email to James Kamensky, with copies to Lexi Graham, Scott Stout, Robert Elliott, and Ashlee Williams, simply noting that he was “circling back again” and asking how things were progressing on the matter.

Earlier that week, on May 7, 2024, Whaley followed up again with James Kamensky, asking whether there were any issues obtaining certain records, and flagging that it had been since February at the very least.

In mid-April 2024, on April 16, James Kamensky replied that the request for records and bills remained in process with University of Louisville (UofL) Hospital in Louisville, Kentucky.

Significantly, in March 2024 there were several exchanges regarding Naomi Robinson and other related bills and records. On March 14, 2024, Lexi Graham, serving as Case Manager, informed the recipients that she had CC’d the handling attorney on Naomi Robinson’s matter, signaling that internal coordination was being managed among the handling attorney, the case team, and the insurer.

Earlier, on March 13, 2024, Scott Stout advised that Daquan Graham/Stout & Heuke had submitted their bills for the matter. His message provided Louisville and Downtown Louisville office contact details for Stout & Heuke Law Office.

Also on March 13, 2024, at 2:41 PM, Aaron Whaley sent a reply to Robert Elliott (with copies to Scott Stout and Lexi Graham, and to Ashlee Williams) asking for updates and noting that they were likely waiting on Naomi Robinson to submit her medical bills.

Shortly thereafter, at 2:44 PM on March 13, 2024, Scott Stout responded, confirming that Daquan Graham/Stout & Heuke had submitted their bills.

Earlier still, on March 6, 2024, Robert Elliott from Liberty Mutual asked for guidance on whether the offices had reached an agreement regarding the distribution of the global policy limit tender to the clients. The thread at that time referenced the policy being underwritten by Liberty Mutual Personal Insurance Company and included the typical attorney–client and work-product confidentiality language found in the signatures of the emails. The messages also contained standard professional signatures with the respective offices’ addresses: Kamensky’s offices in Columbia, South Carolina, and Birmingham, Alabama; and Stout & Heuke’s offices in Louisville, Kentucky; as well as other locations listed in the signatures.

Throughout these communications, the key actors remained the same: Ashlee Williams and the related claimants, Aaron Whaley (Whaley Law Firm), James Kamensky (Kamensky & Patteson, LLP), Lexi Graham (Case Manager), Scott Stout (Stout & Heuke Law Office), and Robert Elliott (Liberty Mutual), with Ashlee Williams also copied on the emails. The underlying themes included obtainingMedical records and bills (notably for Naomi Robinson), the submission of bills by Daquan Graham (on behalf of Stout & Heuke), and efforts to resolve timing and fund distribution questions related to the global policy limit tender.

item_165.note: Case: Ashlee-Williams-MVA-[DOB-555] involves Ashlee Williams following a motor vehicle accident on August 29, 2023, with Daquan Graham, Naomi Robinson, and Julmonzhae Moore also named in the claim. The matter is identified as Claim No. 054658453-01. The recited communications show ongoing settlement discussions among counsel from Whaley Law Firm and Stout & Heuke Law Office, with James Kamensky and Lexi Graham among the recipients and August 2023 accident-related claimants copied on the messages.

The core issue in the correspondence is how to allocate Liberty Mutual’s $50,000 liability limit among the four claimants. Liberty Mutual tendered the full $50,000 to be divided among Daquan Graham, Naomi Robinson, Ashlee Williams, and Julmonzhae Moore, and Ashlee Williams and Julmonzhae Moore were represented by Aaron Whaley. Whaley proposed apportioning the limits using the medical bills as the basis for division and asked whether there were any objections.

In the early exchanges, Whaley reported the following medical-bill amounts: Ashlee Williams had $35,454.24 in medical bills, and Julmonzhae Moore had $29,092.40. He also noted that those figures were being used to inform the proposed apportionment. Lexi Graham informed the group that the handling attorney James Kamensky was cc’d on the email thread. James Kamensky indicated that they were still gathering medical bills for Naomi Robinson and that apportionment based on medical bills would be the general approach, with further advisement to follow once the bills were in. On January 31, 2024, Whaley asked for the amounts of medical bills each client had, reporting that he already had Ashlee Williams at $35,454.24 and Julmonzhae Moore at $29,092.40.

Scott Stout of Stout & Heuke later stated on February 8, 2024 that they were gathering bills and records for Daquan Graham as well and did not object to dividing the settlement based on medical bills. A follow-up on February 12, 2024 confirmed that Daquan Graham’s medical bills were $7,195.00.

By March 1, 2024, Whaley followed up again, noting it was Friday and seeking confirmation that the remaining outstanding medical bills were only those for Naomi Robinson, with the implication that all other medical-bill totals were already identified in the apportionment plan.

In summary, the record shows a four-party claim under Liberty Mutual’s limits, with the proposed method of allocation anchored to medical-bill totals: Ashlee Williams $35,454.24, Julmonzhae Moore $29,092.40, Daquan Graham $7,195.00, and Naomi Robinson’s bills not yet finalized as of the last update. The parties have been coordinating through multiple emails from January through March 2024 to finalize the bill totals and confirm the apportionment method.

item_270.note: Initial client contact on August 29, 2023, with Ashlee Williams regarding a motor vehicle accident that occurred that evening in New Albany, Indiana. The date of the accident is August 29, 2023, at approximately 9:00 PM. The MVA involved P turning left at a green light when the defendant, coming from the opposite direction, ran a red light and t-boned P on the passenger side.

New Albany Police Department responded to the scene, but Ashlee Williams has no information from them. 

Injuries at the scene included a seizure requiring CPR. P sustained injuries to the right arm and right side ribs, and she claims she urinated on herself. She was diagnosed with a concussion and had abdominal bleeding and was unconscious at the scene.

EMS transported her to the University of Louisville (UofL); she was treated at Starlite. 

Employment: Ashlee Williams is employed by UPS as a Package Handler, with an hourly wage of $21. PIP coverage is Liberty Mutual, with no claim information available. P’s vehicle is a 2013 Kia Optima, and the current location of the vehicle is unknown. BI coverage is unknown. Defendant’s vehicle information is unknown.
